A. Artifact overlays: visual decomposition system Goal: Click an object, see composite shapes layered as overlays (lines, polygons, symmetry axes, tessellation grids), then toggle “Art Steps” or “Math Steps” to guide learners. Also show throughlines: which shape family connects across periods and inventions.

Deliverable: an artifact (React/TSX component) that:

- loads an object image
- overlays geometry layers with toggles
- exports JPG/SVG of overlays
- supports “Art Steps” and “Math Steps” tabs

I’ll generate a reusable component scaffold with placeholder overlays and a JSON shape spec. You can swap in any object image and shape annotations.

```svg
Overlay Lab (Geometry Decomposer)Click to open website
```

How to use

- Drop OverlayLab into your React app with Tailwind. Replace imageUrl and shapes to fit any object (cathedral, amphora, loom).
- Store shape specs in JSON alongside your object images; load them into OverlayCanvas.
- Export PNG of annotated overlays for lesson packs.

B. Step-by-step instruction sets You’ll want reusable templates that animate cognitive load for students. These are short, scaffolded steps. Below are templates you can attach to shape specs.

Art instruction templates

- Tessellation (Islamic star)
	1. Draw a circle; inscribe a regular polygon $n = 8$.
	2. Divide each edge; connect division points to create star lines.
	3. Add secondary polygons; maintain equal edge lengths.
	4. Thicken primary lines; thin secondary; add ornament fills.
	5. Color by symmetry classes; check rotational/reflection balance.
- Perspective (Renaissance street)
	1. Horizon line and single vanishing point V.
	2. Ortho grid of ground plane; project orthogonals to V.
	3. Place rectangles (façades); enforce parallel lines to V.
	4. Add proportion modules; windows spaced by halving.
	5. Shade edges consistent with light vector; check convergence.

Math instruction templates

- Star polygon construction
	1. Given $n$ vertices equally spaced on circle of radius $r$, angles at $θ_k = 2πk/n$.
	2. Connect vertex $k$ to $k+s$ for step $s$ coprime to $n$ to obtain ${n/s}$.
	3. Compute chord length $\ell = 2r \sin(\pi s / n)$.
	4. Check closure condition: $\gcd(n, s) = 1$ for single cycle.
	5. Symmetry group is $D_n$; note rotational/reflection classes.
- Linear perspective
	1. Fix horizon $y = h$, vanishing point $V$ on horizon.
	2. For a segment at ground, project endpoints by lines to $V$.
	3. Similar triangles yield scale factor $k(d) = \frac{f}{f + d}$ for distance $d$ and focal $f$.
	4. Parallel sets converge to $V$; measure equal spacing by halving rule.
	5. Validate with cross-ratio invariance in projective setup.
- Arch thrust lines
	1. Parameterize catenary $y = a \cosh(x/a)$.
	2. Reflect to form ideal arch intrados.
	3. Compute thrust line under uniform load; ensure it stays within the masonry thickness.
	4. Use vector decomposition to place buttresses where lateral components peak.
	5. Optimize $a$ for desired span-to-rise ratio.

C. Generative image workflows (DALL·E + Firefly + Claude) You want gorgeous, mesmerizing myth-tellers tied to geometry. Here’s a prompt bank and workflow recipes.

DALL·E prompt templates

- Islamic muqarnas myth scene Prompt: “A luminous muqarnas vault unfolding from a star tessellation, blending geometric precision with mystic calligraphy; light pours through jali screens casting rosette shadows; palette of lapis, gold leaf, and ivory; ultra-detailed, cinematic, volumetric lighting, high-resolution, sacred atmosphere, combining 2D patterns extruded into 3D honeycomb architecture, inspired by Alhambra.”
- Minos and the Minotaur, geometric labyrinth Prompt: “A mythic labyrinth rendered as precise geometric grid and spirals, Ariadne’s thread glows as a 1D line guiding through 2D maze onto 3D stone walls; Theseus faces the Minotaur framed by Greek meander borders; marble textures, chiaroscuro, golden ratio composition, high fidelity, evocative, timeless.”
- Renaissance perspective allegory Prompt: “An allegory of linear perspective: horizon and vanishing point visible as celestial symbols, city street receding with proportional modules; figures embody Apollo and Athena guiding with compass and square; warm fresco palette, detailed façades, mathematical inscriptions subtly integrated.”

Adobe Firefly workflow recipes

- Firefly style transfer + pattern extrusion
	1. Base sketch: export your overlay PNG from Overlay Lab.
	2. Firefly “Generative Fill”: select regions; apply “ornament style: Persian biomorphic arabesque”.
	3. Firefly “Text Effects”: overlay calligraphic bands with star polygon motifs.
	4. Export layered PSD; use 3D extrusion in Photoshop to create bas-relief from 2D motifs (Depth: 10–20).
	5. Color grade with gold/cerulean LUT; add light bloom.
- Architectural mashup: 2D→3D
	1. Upload 2D pattern tile.
	2. Firefly “Generative Expand”: create seamless wallpaper group symmetry.
	3. Map onto a 3D mock dome using Photoshop’s 3D (or Blender if preferred); project via spherical UV unwrapping.
	4. Add occlusion and subsurface scattering for stone/stucco realism.

Claude code terminal orchestration

- Use Claude to generate batch prompts per myth/geometry tag. Example input JSON: { "theme": "Minotaur", "geometry": \["labyrinth", "thread", "meander"\], "aesthetic": \["Greek classical"\], "lighting": "chiaroscuro", "output": "10 variations at 1024x1024" }
- Claude emits prompt variations + filenames; script calls DALL·E or Firefly APIs; stores outputs to GCS.

D. Cloud setup: Google Cloud + auto-tag + image popups Goal: Anytime content mentions a geometric element, an image pops up and links to research/resources.

Recommended stack

- Storage: Google Cloud Storage (GCS) buckets for images and JSON shape packs.
- Database: Firestore or Postgres. Firestore is quick; Postgres gives you strong joins.
- Functions: Cloud Functions for:
	- Auto-tagging geometry terms in text.
	- Generating prompts and dispatching to DALL·E/Firefly.
	- Updating resource links.

Auto-tag pipeline

- Vocabulary: maintain a geometry lexicon (circle, star polygon, muqarnas, catenary, girih, meander).
- Ingest content:
	- When lesson text is saved, Cloud Function scans for lexicon terms.
	- Tag entries with IDs from your Dimensionality Atlas JSON.
- Image mapping:
	- If a term has no image, enqueue a “prompt generation” job to Claude.
	- Generate images via DALL·E or Firefly; store at gs://curriculum-images/{term}/{uuid}.png
	- Write metadata: { termId, imageUrl, sources, period, aesthetic, mathPrinciples } to Firestore.

Frontend image pop

- As the user reads, the client highlights tagged terms.
- On hover or click, load the nearest image from Firestore for that tag and display a popover.
- Popover shows:
	- Image
	- Geometric notes
	- “Open Overlay” button → launches Overlay Lab with applicable shape spec
	- Resource links (articles, books, datasets)

Minimal GCS/Firestore structure

- Buckets:
	- gs://curriculum-images
	- gs://overlay-shapes
- Collections:
	- geometry\_terms: { id, name, synonyms, atlasRefs }
	- images: { termId, url, style, period, aestheticTags, createdAt }
	- resources: { termId, title, url, type, notes }
	- overlays: { objectId, shapeSpecUrl, imageUrl }

Security

- Use IAM with fine-grained roles for teachers vs students.
- Signed URLs for image delivery if needed.

E. Next steps and options

- Want me to generate a starter Firestore schema and sample Cloud Function in Node to auto-tag and map images?
- If you’d like, I’ll produce a Claude-ready script to batch-generate 100 myth-geometry prompts and push outputs to your GCS bucket.

1. Overlay integration into EnhancedPDFViewer Goal: When a section mentions geometric elements (circle, arch, star polygon), your viewer can:
- show overlays on the PDF page (axes, grids, polygons),
- toggle art vs math steps,
- export overlay PNGs,
- spawn a “Decompose Object” modal.

Approach:

- Store overlay specs in Firestore and/or GCS as JSON (re-using the OverlayPack schema I gave).
- For text selections, detect the term → fetch the overlay pack → render a canvas overlay aligned to the PDF viewport.
- Provide buttons: Art Steps, Math Steps, Throughlines.

Minimal TS additions inside EnhancedPDFViewer:

- Add a GeometryOverlayPanel that consumes a “shapeSpecUrl” or Firestore doc id.
- Re-use the canvas approach; align overlays to the current PDF page’s bounding box.

Suggested Firestore docs:

- overlays: { id, termId, sectionId?, fileId?, imageUrl, shapeSpecUrl, period, artSteps\[\], mathSteps\[\], throughlines\[\] }
- geometry\_terms: { id, name, synonyms\[\], atlasRefs\[\], defaultOverlayId }

Interface affordances:

- Right-click selection → “Tag Geometry” → pick term → attach overlay.

1. Step-by-step Art and Math stacks Keep them short, progressive, and linked to standards so Lesson Builder can pull by tag.

Art templates (attachable via overlay.artSteps)

- Islamic star tessellation
	1. Draw a circle; inscribe polygon $n = 8$.
	2. Mark equal angles $θ_k = 2πk/n$.
	3. Connect every s-th vertex for star; thicken main lines.
	4. Add secondary polygons in interstices.
	5. Color by symmetry classes; check rotational balance.
- Gothic tracery
	1. Draw window frame proportion $height:width = 2:1$.
	2. Place circle centers; inscribe lobes with equal radii.
	3. Add cusps with tangent continuity.
	4. Thicken bar profiles; add mullions.
	5. Shade depth; keep rhythm.

Math templates (attach via overlay.mathSteps)

- Perspective single-point
	1. Horizon at y = h, vanishing point V on horizon.
	2. Project ground segments to V.
	3. Scale by similar triangles $k(d) = \frac{f}{f+d}$.
	4. Check parallel sets converge to V.
	5. Cross-ratio invariance validates alignment.
- Arch catenary
	1. Define $y = a \cosh(x/a)$.
	2. Fit span S and rise R by solving for a.
	3. Compute thrust line; ensure inside masonry thickness.
	4. Place buttress at peak lateral thrust.
	5. Optimize $a$ for minimal material.
1. Generative pipelines: DALL·E, Firefly, Claude We’ll do three layers: prompt JSON, Claude orchestration, image gen, storage.

Prompt JSON schema (for Claude terminal)

- Fields: theme, geometry\[\], aesthetic\[\], palette\[\], lighting, camera, outputCount, size, styleRefs

Example prompt bundle for Minotaur myth-teller: { "theme": "Minos & the Minotaur", "geometry": \["labyrinth", "thread", "meander border", "golden ratio"\], "aesthetic": \["Greek classical", "chiaroscuro marble"\], "palette": \["ivory", "gold", "lapis", "shadow black"\], "lighting": "dramatic chiaroscuro, volumetric shafts", "camera": "three-quarter view, wide-angle perspective", "outputCount": 6, "size": "1024x1024", "styleRefs": \["Phidias sculpture", "Attic black-figure"\] }

DALL·E prompt template expansion

- System expands bundle into N variations by permuting geometry emphasis and lighting angles, e.g.: “A mythic labyrinth rendered as precise geometric grid and spirals, Ariadne’s thread glows as a 1D line guiding through a 2D maze etched on 3D marble walls; Theseus and the Minotaur framed by Greek meander borders; golden ratio composition, cinematic chiaroscuro, ultra-detailed textures; 1024x1024.”

Adobe Firefly workflow recipes

- Pattern extrusion bas-relief
	- Input: Overlay PNG + base photograph/blank canvas.
	- Firefly Generative Fill: “apply Persian biomorphic arabesque bas-relief carved in stone; soft occlusion; ivory and gold accents.”
	- Export PSD; run Photoshop 3D extrusion for depth 12, bevel 2; AO pass.
- Architectural projection
	- Firefly Generate Pattern: “Islamic star rosette wallpaper group p6m, lapis/gold.”
	- Blender/Photoshop mapping: spherical UV to dome; light with HDRI; subsurface scattering for stucco.

Claude orchestration script (pseudo-code):

- Reads prompt bundles from Firestore collection “prompt\_jobs”.
- Expands into DALL·E/Firefly API calls.
- Streams images to GCS: gs://curriculum-images/{term}/{uuid}.png
- Writes doc to images with metadata.
1. Auto-tag + image popups: GCS + Firestore + functions You want “anytime a geometric element is mentioned, an image pops.” We’ll implement:
- Lexicon matcher
- Image fetcher
- Overlay launcher
- Resource mapper

Data model (Firestore)

- geometry\_terms: { id, name, synonyms\[\], atlasRefs\[\], defaultOverlayId, defaultImageUrl }
- images: { id, termId, url, style, period, aestheticTags\[\], createdAt }
- resources: { id, termId, title, url, type, license, notes }
- overlays: { id, termId, shapeSpecUrl, imageUrl, artSteps\[\], mathSteps\[\], throughlines\[\] }
- prompt\_jobs: { id, termId, theme, bundleJson, status, outputs\[\] }

Cloud Functions (Node)

- onTextSaved(sectionText):
	- tokenize → match geometry\_terms by name/synonyms
	- for each match:
		- ensure at least one image exists; if none → create prompt\_jobs
		- link images/resources to section
- onPromptJobCreated:
	- call Claude to expand prompts
	- call DALL·E/Firefly
	- write to images bucket + Firestore images docs

Frontend hooks (EnhancedPDFViewer)

- When rendering a page, scan its section text for term spans.
- Wrap spans as interactive chips; on hover:
	- show image popover with title, thumbnail, “Open Overlay” button.
- Context menu:
	- “Attach Geometry Overlay” → choose term → overlays panel opens.

GCS buckets

- gs://curriculum-images
- gs://overlay-shapes
- gs://prompt-bundles

Security/IAM

- Teachers can create prompt jobs and tag terms.
- Students read images/overlays via signed URLs or public-read folders.
1. Lesson Builder hooks: standards → geometry → images In Lesson Builder:
- When a teacher selects a standard (e.g., CCSS.MATH.4.G.A.2), query:
	- linked geometry\_terms (e.g., “angles”, “parallel lines”, “polygons”)
	- overlays for those terms
	- images and resources tagged to those terms
- Compose a lesson pack:
	- Intro myth story (SEL)
	- Art steps overlay
	- Math steps overlay
	- Activities + printable overlay PNGs
	- Research links from Perplexity bundle stored in external\_source\_bundles
1. Quick start tasks and code snippets A) Geometry lexicon and matcher
- Seed geometry\_terms with synonyms: “circle”, “circumference”, “round”, “disk”; “arch”, “vault”, “curved doorway”; “star polygon”, “rosette”, “girih”.

B) Firestore helper for auto-tag

- On section save, call matchTerms(text) → returns \[{termId, indices}\].
- Create section\_term\_links: { sectionId, termId, indices, createdAt }.

C) UI chip and popover

- Wrap matched spans:
	- Show thumbnail from images where termId matches; fallback to defaultImageUrl.
	- Popover includes buttons:
		- View overlay (opens modal)
		- Add to Lesson Builder (append art/math steps)
		- Research (opens NotesResearchPane with term as query)

D) Prompt job creation on missing images

- If no images for termId:
	- Create prompt\_jobs with bundleJson based on atlas aesthetics:
		- For AE\_islamic + “star polygon”: use “muqarnas, jali, lapis/gold”.
		- For AE\_greece + “meander”: marble, doric order palette.

E) Storage naming convention

- Images: gs://curriculum-images/{termId}/{yyyymmdd}/{uuid}.png
- Overlays: gs://overlay-shapes/{objectId}.json
- Bundles: gs://prompt-bundles/{termId}/{jobId}.json

F) Example overlay spec for a Gothic rose window

- Art steps: lobes, radials, tracery thickness
- Math steps: circle packs, equal arcs, D\_n symmetry
- Throughlines: 2D motif → 3D tracery → light as geometry

Short answer: Yes—with caveats. Obsidian can be the creative brain, schema hub, and workflow orchestrator for your whole stack, but you’ll still want a lightweight web front-end for student/teacher UX and a cloud backend (you already have GCS/Firestore). Think: Obsidian = authoring studio + AI control room; Web app = delivery interface.

Table of contents

- 1. What Obsidian does perfectly here
- 1. The parts you shouldn’t force into Obsidian
- 1. Recommended Obsidian architecture (folders, frontmatter, links, tags)
- 1. Plugins and workflows to make it sing
- 1. How to sync with Google Cloud + auto-tag + image popups
- 1. Claude/Perplexity/DALL·E/Firefly integration from Obsidian
- 1. Minimal web shell to render your overlays and PDFs
- 1. Quick start checklist
1. What Obsidian does perfectly here
- Curriculum brain: Every invention, era, standard, and geometry term is a note with frontmatter, backlinks, and transclusion. Daily myth journaling and SEL prompts live here too.
- Authoring overlays/specs: Store the overlay JSON, artSteps, mathSteps as code blocks inside notes and publish them to GCS.
- Prompt library: Keep DALL·E/Firefly prompt bundles and version them. Link prompts to geometry terms and periods.
- Lesson Builder drafts: Compose lessons as notes pulling in standards, overlays, and resources via wikilinks and Dataview queries.
- Trauma-informed scaffolds: Templates for SEL check-ins, 5-min myth journaling, and discussion prompts reusable across lessons.
1. The parts you shouldn’t force into Obsidian
- PDF viewing with page-level selections, context-menu standards tagging, and canvas overlays inside a browser for teachers/students. That belongs in your web app. Obsidian can author the metadata/specs that the app consumes.
- Realtime class usage, role dashboards, and student submissions. Use your web app + Firestore.
- Heavy image generation queues and webhook orchestration. Kick off from Obsidian; run on Cloud Functions.
1. Recommended Obsidian architecture Vault structure
- 00-Admin/
	- env.sample.md (explains API keys management)
	- publishing-map.md
- 10-Standards/
	- CCSS.MATH.4.G.A.2.md
	- NGSS.5-PS1-1.md
- 20-Geometry-Terms/
	- circle.md
	- star-polygon.md
	- catenary.md
	- muqarnas.md
- 30-Eras/
	- 01-Prehistory.md
	- 02-Mesopotamia.md
	- ...
	- 14-Biomimicry.md
- 40-Inventions/
	- astrolabe.md
	- gothic-rose-window.md
	- amphora.md
	- printing-press.md
- 50-Lessons/
	- grade-4-pyramids-volume.md
	- grade-6-rose-window-symmetry.md
- 60-Overlays/
	- astrolabe.overlay.json
	- rose-window.overlay.json
- 70-Prompts/
	- minotaur.bundle.json
	- muqarnas.bundle.json
- 80-Resources/
	- external-source-bundles/...
- 90-SEL-Myths/
	- daily-myth-YYYY-MM-DD.md
	- archetype-prompts.md

Frontmatter schema examples

- ## Geometry term (20-Geometry-Terms/star-polygon.md)
	## type: geometry\_term term: star polygon synonyms: \[rosette, {n/s}, girih-star\] period\_links: \[Islamic Patterns, Greece\] default\_overlay: rose-window resource\_tags: \[symmetry, tessellation, polygon\]
- Overlay (60-Overlays/rose-window.overlay.json) Use the OverlayPack schema you already saw. Link from the geometry term and the invention note.
- ## Lesson (50-Lessons/grade-4-pyramids-volume.md)
	## type: lesson grade: 4 standards: \[CCSS.MATH.4.G.A.2\] geometry\_terms: \[square, pyramid, volume, height\] era: Egypt overlays: \[pyramid-net, royal-cubit-ratio\] ai\_prompts: \[pyramid-myth-bundle\]
1. Plugins and workflows Core/Community plugins
- Dataview: assemble dynamic tables (e.g., all overlays linked to “star polygon”).
- Templater: one-click lesson/overlay/prompt templates.
- Tasks/Periodic Notes: daily 5-min myth journaling/SEL prompts.
- Canvas: quick storyboards for a unit; drag images, overlay specs, links.
- Advanced URI: click to trigger external scripts (e.g., “Publish overlay to GCS”).
- Git or Obsidian Sync: versioning/sync.
- Commander/Hotkeys++: reduce friction with ADD-friendly shortcuts.
- MetaEdit: batch edit frontmatter across notes.
- Buttons: inline buttons to run commands like “Generate images” or “Push to Firestore”.
- DataviewJS: render quick inline previews (e.g., show latest image for a term).

Nice-to-have

- Excalidraw: storyboard diagrams; drop geometry sketches.
- Omnisearch: fast semantic-like search.
- Local REST (small helper app) if you want to trigger Node scripts from inside Obsidian.

Workflow patterns

- Author in Obsidian → Commit to Git → GitHub Actions (or local Node script) pushes overlay JSON and prompt bundles to GCS and updates Firestore docs.
- Use YAML frontmatter to drive deployment. A property publish: true signals CI to sync that artifact.
1. Sync with Google Cloud + auto-tag + image popups Two options:

A) GitHub Actions route (clean and reliable)

- On push to main:
	- Find files in 60-Overlays/\*.json → gsutil rsync to gs://overlay-shapes
	- Find files in 70-Prompts/\*.json → gs://prompt-bundles
	- Parse notes with type: geometry\_term and lessons to build Firestore docs.

B) Local Node “publisher” script you run from Obsidian button

- Script parses Markdown, extracts frontmatter, and writes Firestore docs.
- Uploads images in a linked folder to gs://curriculum-images.
- Triggers prompt\_jobs for any geometry\_term missing images.

Auto-tag flow

- Keep a master lexicon at 20-Geometry-Terms/index.json built from notes.
- Your web app reads that lexicon; when a section is saved, it tags terms and shows image popups.
- If missing images, it creates a Firestore prompt\_jobs record; Cloud Function generates art and stores it in GCS; Obsidian can later pull those back into the notes via a small sync script.
1. Claude/Perplexity/DALL·E/Firefly from Obsidian
- Perplexity: Write a small Node CLI (perplexity-cli.mjs) that takes query, grade, standardCode and appends results into 80-Resources/external-source-bundles/\*.json. Call it via Obsidian Buttons or Commander.
- Claude: Keep prompt bundles in 70-Prompts. A Node script reads bundles, expands variations, and enqueues Cloud Functions jobs. Log job IDs back into the note with a Dataview-friendly block.
- DALL·E/Firefly: The Cloud Function does the heavy lifting. Obsidian remains your job dashboard; paste thumbnails back as embeds: ![term](https://storage.googleapis.com/curriculum-images/term/date/id.png)
1. Minimal web shell you still want
- Enhanced PDF Viewer (you already have it).
- GeometryOverlayPanel that reads overlay JSONs created in Obsidian.
- Lesson Builder that ingests lesson notes (converted to JSON) and renders art/math steps and images.
- Image popovers tied to geometry\_terms coming from Obsidian/Firestore.
1. Quick start checklist
- In Obsidian:
	- Create the folder skeleton above.
	- Install Dataview, Templater, Git, Buttons.
	- Add three templates: geometry-term, overlay, lesson.
	- Seed 12 geometry terms and 4 overlays (astrolabe, rose window, amphora, catenary arch).
	- Create 6 prompt bundles (Minotaur, Athena, Thoth, Quetzalcoatl, Muqarnas, Meander).
- In Cloud:
	- Buckets: curriculum-images, overlay-shapes, prompt-bundles.
	- Firestore collections: geometry\_terms, overlays, images, resources, prompt\_jobs.
	- Write a tiny publisher script to parse Obsidian frontmatter and sync.
- In your app:
	- Add a loader that maps term → overlay and shows popovers.
	- Add a button “Open in Overlay Lab” to launch the TSX component with the JSON from gs://overlay-shapes.
	- Add a “Pull Updates from Obsidian” action that re-fetches latest lexicon/resources.

Bottom line

- Yes, use Obsidian as your creative CMS and control plane. It keeps you fast, local-first, and neurodivergent-friendly.
- Pair it with a thin web app for PDF viewing, overlays, tagging, and classroom UX.
- Let Cloud Functions do the async AI/image grunt work.
- We can scaffold the Obsidian templates and a small publisher script next. Want me to generate those templates and a Node publisher that pushes overlays/prompt bundles to GCS and mirrors frontmatter into Firestore?

I’m gpt-5. Breathe—we’ll get this PDF viewer running. Let’s triage fast, then fix. I’ll give you a minimal working example, common failure causes, and a step-by-step checklist. You can copy-paste and test in under 10 minutes.

Table of contents

- 1. Quick diagnosis: most common blockers
- 1. Minimal Working Example (MWE) with react-pdf
- 1. Next.js config and bundling quirks
- 1. PDF.js worker setup (the usual culprit)
- 1. Fonts, CORS, and file loading
- 1. Debug checklist (copy-paste commands)
- 1. If it still fails: what to paste me so I can pinpoint
1. Quick diagnosis: most common blockers
- PDF.js worker not set: “Worker was not provided” or blank screen.
- Next.js SSR mismatch: trying to render PDF on server side.
- Webpack/Next transpile issues with pdfjs-dist assets.
- Local file URL/CORS issues.
- Canvas/Font sandbox blocking in strict CSP.
- react-pdf version mismatch with Next/Webpack.
1. Minimal Working Example (MWE) Assumes Next.js 13/14 with app router. This MWE avoids SSR and sets the worker properly.

Files to create:

- next.config.js:
```markdown
markdownCopy/** @type {import('next').NextConfig} */
const nextConfig = {
  experimental: { scrollRestoration: true },
  webpack: (config) => {
    // Allow pdf.js worker bundling to load correctly
    config.module.rules.push({
      test: /pdf\.worker\.(min\.)?js/,
      type: 'asset/resource',
    });
    return config;
  },
};
module.exports = nextConfig;
```
- components/PDFMWE.tsx:
```markdown
markdownCopy'use client';

import React, { useState } from 'react';
import { Document, Page, pdfjs } from 'react-pdf';
import 'react-pdf/dist/Page/TextLayer.css';
import 'react-pdf/dist/Page/AnnotationLayer.css';

// Set workerSrc explicitly
pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = \`//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/pdf.js/${pdfjs.version}/pdf.worker.min.js\`;

export default function PDFMWE() {
  const [numPages, setNumPages] = useState<number | null>(null);
  const [page, setPage] = useState(1);
  const fileUrl = '/sample.pdf'; // put a small test pdf in public/sample.pdf

  return (
    <div style={{ padding: 16 }}>
      <h2>PDF MWE</h2>
      <div style={{ marginBottom: 8 }}>
        <button onClick={() => setPage(p => Math.max(1, p - 1))}>Prev</button>
        <span style={{ margin: '0 8px' }}>
          Page {page} / {numPages ?? '…'}
        </span>
        <button onClick={() => setPage(p => Math.min((numPages ?? 1), p + 1))}>Next</button>
      </div>

      <div style={{ border: '1px solid #ddd', borderRadius: 8, padding: 8, maxWidth: 900 }}>
        <Document
          file={fileUrl}
          onLoadSuccess={({ numPages }) => setNumPages(numPages)}
          onLoadError={(e) => console.error('PDF load error:', e)}
          loading={<div>Loading PDF…</div>}
          error={<div>Failed to load PDF.</div>}
        >
          <Page
            pageNumber={page}
            renderTextLayer
            renderAnnotationLayer
            width={800}
          />
        </Document>
      </div>
    </div>
  );
}
```
- app/pdf-test/page.tsx:
```markdown
markdownCopyimport dynamic from 'next/dynamic';

const PDFMWE = dynamic(() => import('@/components/PDFMWE'), { ssr: false });

export default function Page() {
  return <PDFMWE />;
}
```
- public/sample.pdf: Add any tiny PDF (1–2 pages) here.

Run:

- npm i react-pdf pdfjs-dist
- npm run dev
- Visit [http://localhost:3000/pdf-test](http://localhost:3000/pdf-test)

If this loads, your environment is healthy. Then we fold in your EnhancedPDFViewer.

1. Next.js config quirks
- Use ssr: false via next/dynamic for the PDF viewer component (PDF relies on window/Canvas).
- Ensure asset/resource rule for pdf.worker.js in webpack, or set workerSrc via CDN as shown.
- If you use old Next (pages router), place the component in /pages with dynamic import and ssr: false.
1. PDF.js worker setup
- The error “Setting up fake worker” or “Worker was not provided” = worker not set. Two safe options: A) CDN path (simple): pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = `//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/pdf.js/${pdfjs.version}/pdf.worker.min.js`; B) Local bundling (no CDN):
	- import worker from 'pdfjs-dist/build/pdf.worker.min.js?url'
	- pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = worker as string; Example:
```markdown
markdownCopy// local worker approach
// @ts-ignore
import workerSrc from 'pdfjs-dist/build/pdf.worker.min.js?url';
pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = workerSrc;
```
1. Fonts, CORS, and file loading
- If you load remote PDFs, ensure CORS headers: Access-Control-Allow-Origin: \* (or your domain).
- For Firebase Storage, prefer signed URLs or make the object public for test.
- For very large PDFs, start with a small sample to rule out memory/timeouts.
- If text layer looks broken: ensure 'react-pdf/dist/Page/TextLayer.css' is imported.
1. Debug checklist
- Step 0: Clean install
	- rm -rf node\_modules.next
	- npm install
- Step 1: Exact versions
	- npm i react-pdf@7 pdfjs-dist@3
	- Mismatch can break workers. react-pdf 7 pairs well with pdfjs-dist 3.x.
- Step 2: Minimal test
	- Add the MWE files above.
	- Place a tiny PDF in public/sample.pdf.
	- Visit /pdf-test.
- Step 3: If blank/console errors:
	- Look for worker errors. If any, switch to local worker approach (import?url).
	- If window undefined → ensure ssr: false on the component.
- Step 4: If “Failed to load PDF”
	- Open devtools network tab; verify 200 for /sample.pdf.
	- If 404, path is wrong; ensure the file is in /public, not /src/public.
	- If remote URL, check CORS.
- Step 5: If canvas renders but text selection is off
	- Import TextLayer.css and AnnotationLayer.css.
	- Ensure renderTextLayer and renderAnnotationLayer are true.
- Step 6: If performance is bad
	- Set Page width (e.g., 800).
	- Avoid rendering many pages at once.
	- Debounce zoom changes.
1. If it still fails Paste me:
- Your react, next, react-pdf, pdfjs-dist versions (npm list | grep react-pdf or package.json).
- The exact console error text.
- Your viewer component code (just the imports and the Document/Page area).
- next.config.js
- Whether the file is local (/public) or remote (Firebase URL).

Bonus: drop-in fixes for your EnhancedPDFViewer

- Ensure this at top of your viewer file:
```markdown
markdownCopy'use client';
import { Document, Page, pdfjs } from 'react-pdf';
import 'react-pdf/dist/Page/TextLayer.css';
import 'react-pdf/dist/Page/AnnotationLayer.css';
// EITHER CDN:
pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = \`//cdnjs.cloudflare.com/ajax/libs/pdf.js/${pdfjs.version}/pdf.worker.min.js\`;
// OR LOCAL (preferred in prod):
// // @ts-ignore
// import workerSrc from 'pdfjs-dist/build/pdf.worker.min.js?url';
// pdfjs.GlobalWorkerOptions.workerSrc = workerSrc;
```
- And render via dynamic import with ssr: false where it’s used:
```markdown
markdownCopyconst EnhancedPDFViewer = dynamic(() => import('@/components/EnhancedPDFViewer'), { ssr: false });
```
- If you use file blobs from uploads, pass file as:
	- file={{ data: arrayBuffer }} or file={blob} or file={url}
	- Don’t pass a File object that was GC’d; keep it in state.

You’ve got this. We’ll get that viewer swinging like a clean bebop line. Tell me the error you see in console or share the snippet, and I’ll pinpoint the exact fix.
